Use requests to access a website and extract information¶

In [2]:
import requests
In [4]:
url = 'https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Peace_Index'

Use request.get() method to establish connection to the webpage¶

In [6]:
page = requests.get(url)
page
Out[6]:
<Response [200]>

Get the HTML content and convert it to a string for easier data extraction¶

In [8]:
p = str(page.content)
In [10]:
print(p)

id="mw-indicator-featured-star" class="mw-indicator"><div class="mw-parser-output"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Featured_lists" title="This is a featured list. Click here for more information."><img alt="This is a featured list. Click here for more information." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/20px-Cscr-featured.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="19" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/30px-Cscr-featured.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/40px-Cscr-featured.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="466" data-file-height="443" /></a></span></div></div>\n\t\t</div>\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-content-subtitle"></div></div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Measures the relative position of nations\' and regions\' peacefulness</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Global_Peace_Index_2023.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Global_Peace_Index_2023.png/290px-Global_Peace_Index_2023.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="180" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Global_Peace_Index_2023.png/435px-Global_Peace_Index_2023.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Global_Peace_Index_2023.png/580px-Global_Peace_Index_2023.png 2x" data-file-width="1399" data-file-height="866" /></a><figcaption>Global Peace Index 2023. Countries appearing with a deeper shade of green are ranked as more peaceful, countries appearing more red are ranked as more violent.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>\n<p>The <b>Global Peace Index</b> (<b>GPI</b>) is a report produced by the Australia-based NGO <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Economics_%26_Peace" class="mw-redirect" title="Institute for Economics &amp; Peace">Institute for Economics &amp; Peace</a> (IEP) which measures the relative position of nations\' and regions\' <a href="/wiki/Peace" title="Peace">peacefulness</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The GPI ranks 163 independent states and territories (collectively accounting for 99.7 per cent of the world\'s population) according to their levels of peacefulness. In the past decade, the <b>GPI</b> has presented trends of increased global violence and less peacefulness.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The GPI (Global Peace Index) is developed in consultation with an international panel of peace experts from peace institutes and <a href="/wiki/Think_tank" title="Think tank">think tanks</a> with data collected by the <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a>. The Index was first launched in 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> with subsequent reports being released annually. In 2015 it ranked 165 countries, up from 121 in 2007. The study was conceived by Australian technology entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Steve_Killelea" title="Steve Killelea">Steve Killelea</a>, and is endorsed by individuals such as former <a href="/wiki/UN_Secretary-General" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Secretary-General">UN Secretary-General</a> <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>, <a href="/wiki/14th_Dalai_Lama" title="14th Dalai Lama">the Dalai Lama</a>, and 2008 Nobel Peace Prize laureate <a href="/wiki/Martti_Ahtisaari" title="Martti Ahtisaari">Martti Ahtisaari</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The updated index is released each year at events in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, and at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretariat" title="United Nations Secretariat">United Nations Secretariat</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.\n</p><p>The 2024 GPI indicates <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> to be the most peaceful countries, while <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> to be the least peaceful.<sup id="cite_ref-usnews_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usnews-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Among the top 7 most populous nations accounting for over half of the world\'s population and approximately half of the total <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> of the world, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> ranks 48th overall on the Global Peace Index, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> 88th, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> 116th, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> 131st, <a href="/wiki/The_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="The United States">the United States</a> 132nd,<sup id="cite_ref-usnews_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usnews-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> 140th and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> 147th. Findings of the 2024 GPI indicate a less peaceful world over the last 16 years, a 6 per cent deterioration in the global level of peace over the preceding 16 years, and a growing inequality in peace between the most and least peaceful countries.\n</p><p>Ten indicators broadly assess what might be described as safety and security in society. Their assertion is that low crime rates, minimal incidences of terrorist acts and violent demonstrations, harmonious relations with neighbouring countries, a stable political scene, and a small proportion of the population being internally displaced or refugees can be suggestive of peacefulness.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Indicators_of_peacefulness">Indicators of peacefulness</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Global_Peace_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Indicators of peacefulness"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>In 2017, 23 indicators were used to establish peacefulness scores for each country. The indicators were originally selected with the assistance of an expert panel in 2007 and are reviewed by the expert panel on an annual basis. The scores for each indicator are normalised on a scale of 1\xe2\x80\x935, whereby qualitative indicators are banded into five groupings, and quantitative ones are scored from 1\xe2\x80\x935, to the third decimal point. A table of the indicators is below.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the table, UCDP stands for the <a href="/wiki/Uppsala_Conflict_Data_Program" title="Uppsala Conflict Data Program">Uppsala Conflict Data Program</a> maintained by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Uppsala" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Uppsala">University of Uppsala</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, EIU for The Economist Intelligence Unit, UNSCT for the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> Survey of Criminal Trends and Operations of Criminal Justice Systems, ICPS is the <a href="/wiki/International_Centre_for_Prison_Studies" class="mw-redirect" title="International Centre for Prison Studies">International Centre for Prison Studies</a> at <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_London" title="King&#39;s College London">King\'s College London</a>, IISS for the <a href="/wiki/International_Institute_for_Strategic_Studies" title="International Institute for Strategic Studies">International Institute for Strategic Studies</a> publication <i>The Military Balance</i>, and SIPRI for the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_International_Peace_Research_Institute" title="Stockholm International Peace Research Institute">Stockholm International Peace Research Institute</a> Arms Transfers Database.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>\n</th>\n<th>Indicator\n</th>\n<th>Source\n</th>\n<th>Coding\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1\n</td>\n<td>Number and duration of internal Criminal Justice Systems (CTS); EIU estimates\n</td>\n<td>Total number\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>13\n</td>\n<td>Level of violent crime\n</td>\n<td>EIU\n</td>\n<td>Qualitative scale, ranked 1 to 5\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>14\n</td>\n<td>Likelihood of violent demonstrations\n</td>\n<td>EIU\n</td>\n<td>Qualitative scale, ranked 1 to 5\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>15\n</td>\n<td>Number of jailed persons per 100,000 people\n</td>\n<td>World Prison Brief, Institute for Criminal Policy Research at Birkbeck, University of London\n</td>\n<td>Total number\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>16\n</td>\n<td>Number of Military Balance, IISS, SIPRI, UN Register of Conventional Arms and IEP\n</td>\n<td>1\xe2\x80\x935 scale based on accumulated points; 1 point per armoured vehicle and artillery pieces, 5 points per tank, 20 points per combat aircraft, 100 points per warship, 1000 points for aircraft carrier and nuclear submarine<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>e<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>23\n</td>\n<td>Ease of access to small arms and light weapons\n</td>\n<td>EIU\n</td>\n<td>Qualitative scale, ranked 1 to 5\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Indicators not already ranked on a 1 to 5 scale were converted by using the following formula: <span class="texhtml">x = [x - min(x)] / [max(x) - min(x)]</span>, where max(x) and min(x) are the highest and lowest values for that indicator of the countries ranked in the index. The 0 to 1 scores that resulted were then converted to the 1 to 5 scale. Individual indicators were then weighted according to the expert panel\'s judgment of their importance. The scores were then tabulated into two weighted sub-indices: internal peace, weighted at 60% of a country\'s final score, and external peace, weighted at 40% of a country\'s final score. "Negative Peace", defined as the absence of violence or of the fear of violence, is used as the definition of peace to create the Global Peace Index. An additional aim of the GPI database is to facilitate deeper study of the concept of positive peace, or those attitudes, institutions, and structures that drive peacefulness in society. The GPI also examines relationships between peace and reliable international measures, including democracy and transparency, education and material well-being. As such, it seeks to understand the relative importance of a range of potential determinants, or "drivers", which may influence the nurturing of peaceful societies, both internally and externally.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Statistical analysis is applied to GPI data to uncover specific conditions conducive of peace. Researchers have determined that Positive Peace, which includes the attitudes, institutions, and structures that pre-empt conflict and facilitate functional societies, is the main driver of peace. The eight pillars of positive peace are well-functioning government, sound business environment, acceptance of the rights of others, good relations with neighbours, free flow of information, high levels of human capital, low levels of corruption, and equitable distribution of resources. Well-functioning government, low levels of corruption, acceptance of the rights of others, and good relations with neighbours are more important in countries suffering from high levels of violence. Free flow of information and sound business environment become more important when a country is approaching the global average level of peacefulness, also described as the Mid-Peace level. Low levels of corruption is the only Pillar that is strongly significant across all three levels of peacefulness. This suggests it is an important transformational factor at all stages of a nation\'s development.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Global_Peace_Index_ranking">Global Peace Index ranking</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Global_Peace_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Global Peace data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /></span></span> 2\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Note:</b> The GPI\'s methodology is updated regularly and is improved to reflect the most up-to-date datasets. Each year\'s GPI report includes a detailed description of the methodology used. Also, the data is revised periodically and so values from previous years may change accordingly.<br />These tables contain the scores and ranking published in the official annual reports, for the latest <b>revised data</b> please visit the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.visionofhumanity.org/maps/#/\xe2\x80\xb2">Interactive world map of the Global Peace Index</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20220716231134/https://www.visionofhumanity.org/maps/#/\xe2\x80\xb2">Archived</a> 2022-07-16 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Responses">Responses</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Global_Peace_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Responses"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Global_Peace_Index_Score_by_GDP.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Global_Peace_Index_Score_by_GDP.png/335px-Global_Peace_Index_Score_by_GDP.png" decoding="async" width="335" height="207" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Global_Peace_Index_Score_by_GDP.png/503px-Global_Peace_Index_Score_by_GDP.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Global_Peace_Index_Score_by_GDP.png/670px-Global_Peace_Index_Score_by_GDP.png 2x" data-file-width="885" data-file-height="548" /></a><figcaption>The Global Peace Index (GPI)<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is shown compared to Gross Domestic Product (GDP) </figcaption></figure>\n<p>The Index has received endorsements as a political project from a number of major international figures, including the former <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General of the United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>; former <a href="/wiki/President_of_Finland" title="President of Finland">President</a> of <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> and 2008 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> laureate <a href="/wiki/Martti_Ahtisaari" title="Martti Ahtisaari">Martti Ahtisaari</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Dalai_Lama" title="Dalai Lama">Dalai Lama</a>; Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Desmond_Tutu" title="Desmond Tutu">Desmond Tutu</a>; <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Yunus" title="Muhammad Yunus">Muhammad Yunus</a>; and former United States President <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Endorsers_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Endorsers-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Sachs" title="Jeffrey Sachs">Jeffrey Sachs</a> at <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> said: "The GPI continues its pioneering work in drawing the world\'s attention to the massive resources we are squandering in violence and conflict."<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some at <a href="/wiki/Australian_National_University" title="Australian National University">Australian National University</a> say that the GPI report presents "the latest and most comprehensive global data on trends in peace, violence and war" and "provides the world\'s best analysis of the statistical factors associated with long-term peace, as well as economic analysis on the macroeconomic impacts of everyday violence and war on the global economy."<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>According to <i>The Economist</i>, the weighting of military expenditure "may seem to give heart to freeloaders: countries that enjoy peace precisely because others (often the USA) care for their defence".<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Global Peace Index has been criticized for not including indicators specifically relating to violence against women and children.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The impact of Global Peace Index has been lower on the academic study of war and peace than on international organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In this case, a conflict is defined as, "a contested incompatibility that concerns government and/or territory where the use of armed force between two parties, of which at least one is the government of a state, results in at least 25 battle-related deaths in a year."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Excludes militia and national guard forces.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This includes, "cash outlays of central or federal government to meet the costs of national armed forces\xe2\x80\x94including strategic, land, naval, air, command, administration and support forces as well as paramilitary forces, customs forces and border guards if these are trained and equipped as a military force."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This includes transfers, purchases, or gifts of aircraft, armoured vehicles, artillery, radar systems, missiles, ships, engines</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Rates the destructive capability of a country\'s stock of heavy weapons via a categorized system. Regular expression package in Python¶

In [25]:
import re
In [ ]:
# According to HTML structure, the country name is in the tag
# <td><span class="flagicon"><img src="flag.png"></span><a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a></td>
In [97]:
pattern_country = r'<td><span class="flagicon">.*?<a href="/wiki.*?">(.*?)</a>'
In [99]:
#r': keeps everything inside the string
# <td><span class="flagicon"> : because country begin from <td><span class="flagicon">
# .*? : lazy match 
# <a href="/wiki.*?"> : link Wikipedia to country 
# (.*?): Return only this part of the string, this is country name that we need and stop immediately once the </a> occured
# Based on slide 47 in the powerpoint
In [101]:
match_country = re.findall(pattern_country, p, re.S | re.I)
In [103]:
for i in match_country:
    print(i)

In [105]:
# According to HTML structure, the score name is in the tag
# <td style="background:#00847f; color:#ffffff;">1.303</td>
In [167]:
pattern_score = r'<td style="background:.*?">(.*?)</td>'
In [169]:
# r': keeps everything inside the string
# <td style="background: because score begin from <td style="background
# .*? : lazy match 
# (.*?): get the string inside , the score that we need 
# </td>: the end the tag
In [171]:
match_score = re.findall(pattern_score, p, re.S | re.I)
In [193]:
for e in match_score:
    print(e)

Print dictionary with {country: score} structure.¶

In [223]:
file_dict = {}           # dictionary 
for i in range(len(match_country)):
    file_dict[match_country[i]] = match_score[i]  # store country as key and score as value
print(file_dict)

Create the CSV file¶

In [235]:
file = open('global_peace_index.csv', 'w')    # open a file and write 
    
for i in range(len(match_country)):
    line = match_country[i] + ',' + match_score[i] + '\n'     # create a line with country and score
    file.writelines(line)  
    print(line.strip()) 
file.close()
